</details>

### The SDR-to-AE handoff leak
- **What it is:** The SDR books a qualified meeting. Context lives in the SDR's head. The AE takes the call cold, the prospect repeats themselves, the energy the SDR built evaporates, and the deal loses momentum at the exact moment it should accelerate.
- **Why there's no good answer:** CRM notes never capture what actually made the prospect lean in. The mediocre fix: a handoff template and a joint call — but templates flatten nuance and joint calls don't scale. The living context of why-this-person-is-interested is the hardest thing to transfer between two humans.

<details><summary><b>AI prompt — think it through</b></summary>

The mediocre fix: a handoff template and a joint call — but templates flatten nuance and joint calls don't scale. The living context of why-this-person-is-interested is the hardest thing to transfer between two humans.


</details>

### Comp plans that reward the wrong thing
- **What it is:** You pay on meetings booked, so reps book bad meetings. You pay on pipeline, so they inflate pipeline. You pay on closed revenue only, so they hoard and sandbag. Every metric you comp becomes a target that gets gamed.
- **Why there's no good answer:** Goodhart's law is undefeated: when a measure becomes a target, it stops being a good measure. No comp plan escapes it. The mediocre fix: change the plan every year to stay ahead of the gaming — which destroys the trust and predictability that comp is supposed to provide.

<details><summary><b>AI prompt — think it through</b></summary>

```

The mediocre fix: change the plan every year to stay ahead of the gaming — which destroys the trust and predictability that comp is supposed to provide.

```

</details>

### Forecasting on dirty data
- **What it is:** Leadership needs a number. The number is built on CRM stages that reps update inconsistently, close dates that are fiction, and 'commit' deals based on optimism. The forecast is a confident number resting on sand.
- **Why there's no good answer:** You can't forecast accurately from data that's entered by people incentivized to make it look good. The mediocre fix: a manager 'sandbags the sandbaggers' by mental adjustment — replacing dirty data with a gut feel that's also biased. Everyone knows the forecast is partly fiction and reports it anyway.

<details><summary><b>AI prompt — think it through</b></summary>

The mediocre fix: a manager 'sandbags the sandbaggers' by mental adjustment — replacing dirty data with a gut feel that's also biased. Everyone knows the forecast is partly fiction and reports it anyway.


</details>

### The rep who's great in person, terrible in the CRM
- **What it is:** Your best closer builds real relationships and wins deals nobody else could — and logs nothing, so their pipeline is invisible, their deals can't be coached, and when they leave, all that context walks out the door.
- **Why there's no good answer:** Forcing the process kills the thing that makes them great; not forcing it means you're blind. No manager fully solves this. The mediocre fix: a junior 'deal coordinator' who logs behind them — expensive, and it treats a symptom. The tension between human selling and systematized selling never fully resolves.

<details><summary><b>AI prompt — think it through</b></summary>


</details>

### When the founder is the only one who can sell it
- **What it is:** Early deals close because the founder sells them — with conviction, context, and authority no rep can replicate. Then you hire reps, and the motion doesn't transfer, because half of what worked was 'the founder personally cares.'
- **Why there's no good answer:** Founder-led sales is real and largely non-transferable. The mediocre fix: record everything the founder does and try to systematize it — but you can't systematize authority or genuine conviction. Most companies stall here for a year figuring out what actually transfers and what doesn't.

<details><summary><b>AI prompt — think it through</b></summary>

---

# The through-line

Center to edge, the whole map says one thing: the craft evolves, but the intention underneath stays human. The fundamentals never stop mattering. AI amplifies reach but does not supply the intention. Some problems stay hard no matter how the tools change.

The prompts in this guide are the bridge from the map to the mirror — from seeing the craft whole to becoming capable at it, one skill at a time, grounded in your own calls.

_The intention of effort · Nithin Nair_
